Important News

Zhang Hailpeng's Army Collapses 64

Peng and Xu, Two Regiment Commanders, Defect

Fighting on the Tao'an-Ang'angxi Railway Has Ceased

Harbin Correspondence: The most intense fighting on the Tao'an-Ang'angxi Railway occurred on the nights of the 14th and 16th. Yu Zhaolin's brigade blew up two Jiangqiao bridges. The largest railway bridge over the Nen River was prepared with buried mines to be detonated when Zhang's army advanced. However, as the fighting commenced, Yu's army gained the upper hand, and Zhang's troops failed to advance, allowing the bridge to be preserved. On the evening of the 15th, Zhang's army, with the assistance of Japanese armored vehicles, launched a fierce attack, but was soon repelled by Yu's brigade. Fighting resumed at noon on the 16th, with three Japanese aircraft providing aerial cover and dropping bombs. Yu's brigade suffered heavy casualties and was in a precarious situation. Fortunately, the Sun and Wang infantry regiments of the Xing'an Reclamation Army arrived from the Mongolian border, threatening to attack Zhang's army from the rear. Zhang, concerned about his rear, reduced his attacking force. In the evening, the armored vehicles returned, unleashing heavy artillery fire, with machine guns and mortars bombarding heavily. Fortunately, Yu's brigade managed to destroy the armored vehicle's locomotive with artillery fire, thwarting Zhang's efforts. There were minor clashes early on the 17th, but they soon ceased. On that day, internal changes occurred within Zhang's army. The Peng and Xu infantry regiments resolutely defected, refusing to obey Zhang's command and planning to return to attack Tao'an. At the same time, Huang Xiansheng, the former commander of the 24th Northeastern Army, arrived in Tao'an from Jinzhou to incorporate the Peng and Xu regiments. With Zhang's strength diminished, he dared not advance further. Due to wavering morale, a large number of Mongolian troops deserted and scattered. Consequently, Zhang retreated to Tao'an at noon on the 18th. Before retreating, he abducted many railway workers along the Tao'an-Ang'angxi line, reportedly to incorporate them into his forces to replenish his strength for a future resurgence. The Japanese troops in Tao'an, originally numbering 300, upon hearing news of the Peng and Xu regiments' plan to attack Tao'an, specially dispatched a regiment each of artillery and infantry from Sipingjie and Gongzhuling to Tao'an on the 18th to help Zhang defend the area. Currently, the Heilongjiang army and the allied Sun, Wang, Peng, and Xu regiments have established an impregnable defensive line on the Tao'an-Ang'angxi Railway. Even if Zhang's army attacks again, it is unlikely to succeed. Ma Zhanshan, the acting chairman of Heilongjiang Province, sent telegrams from Heihe to various brigades, ordering them to firmly defend the Tao'an-Ang'angxi line and prohibiting retreat, otherwise they would be executed. The Su Bingwen brigade of the 2nd Heilongjiang Infantry Brigade stationed in Hailar, along with the Wu Songshan regiment of the 1st Cavalry Brigade, have arrived in succession at Fularji Station to defend the Dongping County area and prevent Zhang's army from attacking from that direction. Another regiment of the Su brigade, along with the Zhang Zhanjiu regiment of the 2nd Cavalry Brigade and the Wu Songshan regiment, are stationed at Ang'angxi Station as a general reserve force. The Li Qingshan regiment of Ma Zhanshan's infantry departed from Tonghe County by boat on the 19th for Harbin. Once all troops have arrived, they will be dispatched to Heihe in the next day or two to reinforce defenses. Recently, militia groups have been established in various counties under Heilongjiang's jurisdiction. If necessary, some can be mobilized to assist the army in defending everything. Ma Zhanshan himself was initially reported to have entered Heihe to assume the chairmanship, but this has recently been proven inaccurate. Ma departed from Heihe by boat on the 11th and arrived in Harbin early on the 19th. He secretly traveled from Harbin to Heihe with his adjutant and chief of staff. Very few people knew about it until Ma arrived in Heilongjiang Province. Zhao Zhongren, Dou Lianfang, and Liang Heng, the police chief of the provincial capital, who had previously taken refuge in Harbin, have returned to Heilongjiang Province yesterday because Heihe has been stabilized. Regarding the defection of the Peng and Xu regiments of Zhang Hailpeng's army, it is said that Zhang was hesitant and undecided at the beginning of his invasion of Heilongjiang due to numerous concerns. After repeated pressure from the Japanese consul, 300 Japanese soldiers came to surround Zhang's military governor's office on the 12th, forcing Zhang to order mobilization. Zhang then summoned the Peng and Xu regiment commanders and ordered them to prepare for departure to Heilongjiang. The two regiment commanders kowtowed and said, "We dare not disobey the military governor's order. However, if the regiment commanders see the military governor again, it will be when they are presenting his head." Zhang, believing that the two regiment commanders had always been obedient, did not suspect anything else. However, the two regiment commanders delayed their advance after departing, and later defected. The two regiments were originally part of Huang Xiansheng's old 24th Brigade. Now that Huang has come to incorporate them, the two regiment commanders naturally expressed their obedience. With the fighting concluded, it is reported that traffic on the Tao'an-Ang'angxi Railway will resume between Tailai and Ang'angxi starting from the 20th. (19th)

Jilin Generals Refuse Xi Qia's Puppet Orders 65

Xi Qia Flatters the Japanese, Displaying Utmost Servility

Merchants and Civilians Unable to Endure Oppression Flee in Droves

Harbin Correspondence: After Xi Qia, under Japanese orders, reorganized the Jilin Provincial Government, he converted all provincial troops into security brigades, with each brigade commander serving as a security commander. However, most brigade and regimental commanders disdained Xi Qia's actions and refused to obey orders and be incorporated. Only a portion of Zhang Zuozhou's 25th Jilin Army stationed in the provincial capital was disarmed because they were unable to retreat when the Japanese army arrived in Jilin. Xi reorganized them into the 1st Infantry Regiment of the 1st Security Brigade, with many former officials being replaced. He also transferred Li Guilin, the former commander of the 23rd Brigade stationed in Changchun, to serve as the brigade commander. Xi assigned Qi Zhizheng, a former military advisor, to incorporate Li's troops and reorganize them into the 2nd Security Brigade. However, although Li Guilin resides in Changchun, within the sphere of Japanese influence, he remains steadfast and refuses to accept Xi's puppet orders. Qi Zhizheng arrived in Changchun on the 16th of this month to take over, but was rejected by Li. Therefore, Xi's Jilin administrator is merely a figurehead. Xi is quite anxious. He recently sent two staff officers, Li and Wu, with a letter to Yushu to meet Zhang Zuozhou, commander of the 25th Brigade, instructing him to hand over all military power, otherwise Zhang's family and property in the province would not be protected. However, Li and Wu have been gone for half a month and have not returned. The unarmed soldiers of the brigade reorganized by Xi have also recently secretly gone to Yushu to rejoin their former brigade commander. Xi also sent Zhai Jingru, the director of the timber and stone tax bureau in the provincial capital, to persuade Li Du, the garrison commander of Yilan, and Ding Qu and Xing Qingzhan in Harbin. After Zhai arrived in Harbin and learned that Ding and Xing's attitude was anti-Xi, he did not dare to show his face and went to Yilan. However, he also failed to achieve his objective. Therefore, Xi Qia's administrator only exercises his power in the Jilin provincial capital. Although Xi previously declared that he would temporarily maintain order in Jilin and not attach himself to any party, he recently appointed Jin Bi'dong, the son of the former Prince Su of the Qing dynasty, as the head of the Changchun Municipal Preparatory Office and the director of the Jichang and Jidun railways. At the same time, he sent a Japanese advisor, Sanqiao, by plane to Shenyang to participate in the restorationist conference convened by Prince Gong in Shenyang on the 20th of this month. Furthermore, the Jichang and Jihai railways were originally not connected because the Jilin authorities, when constructing the Jihai railway, intended to prevent the two railways from being jointly operated and to prevent them from becoming feeder lines for the South Manchuria Railway. Therefore, the tracks of the two railways were 365 meters apart. Xi Qia has now listened to the Japanese and has started work on connecting the tracks on the 18th of this month. It is expected to be completed in about half a month. The South Manchuria Railway has already connected the Shenhai railway with this line. Now that the Jihai railway is also connected, a Japanese railway network has been formed. Previously (on the 15th), Honjo arrived in Jilin to inspect the troops. Xi Qia led his subordinates to the station to greet him, and in the evening, he held a grand banquet to entertain him. His flattery was like that of a servant to his master. The next day, Xi even fabricated news, saying that Honjo had ordered the Japanese army to retreat to Lianhua Pao outside the city, in order to reassure the people. However, Honjo went to Changchun that evening, and the Japanese army remains stationed in Jilin to this day. Japanese military police, wanting to confiscate firearms from merchants and civilians, have been conducting daily inspections, breaking into homes late at night. If the owners are slow to respond, they are either killed by bayonets or beaten and injured. The suffering of merchants and civilians is worse than that of a conquered people. As a result, they would rather abandon their homes and businesses and flee to other cities. The number of people fleeing Jilin in recent days is no less than that of Shenyang. (19th)

Ma Longtan Declares Himself Chairman of the Sino-Manchurian Association

Zhao Xinbo Illegally Seizes Northeastern Legal Authority

Weng Enyu Takes Over the Liaoning Finance Department

Ma Longtan, Tianjin Dispatch: After the Japanese army occupied Liaoning and Jilin, they declared to the international community that they had no intention of aggression against Chinese territory and that they guaranteed the integrity of Chinese territory. In reality, they are supporting the establishment of new regimes in various regions, instigating the independence of various counties. The Japanese are actively promoting the so-called "small autonomy movement" without any relaxation. In addition to Tieling, Fushun, and other counties that have already declared autonomy, and Sipingjie, which has been established as a city, implementing everything under the direction of Japanese advisors, they also planned to carve out the six counties of Lishu, Changtu, Kaiyuan, Huaide, Tongliao, and Liaoyuan to establish the so-called Sino-Manchurian Province. However, the Japanese now believe that establishing a province is too ambitious and fear opposition from China and the international community. Therefore, they have abandoned the idea of the Sino-Manchurian Province and are instead encouraging the five counties of Changtu, Lishu, Liaoyuan, Huaide, and Kaiyuan to organize a Sino-Manchurian United Independent Autonomy Association to avoid the name of a province while achieving the reality of a province. Tongliao County, located in western Liaoning, is difficult to control. Therefore, only the five counties of Changtu, etc., have united. The association was established on the 15th in Sipingjie, with Ma Longtan as the chairman. It was named the "Sino-Manchurian United Independent Autonomy Association," and its address was set up in the Hongwanzi (Red Swastika) Society compound. Ma Longtan issued an absurd and incoherent declaration, which is recorded below (verbatim, without any deletions or modifications). Declaration: In view of the fact that since the Sino-Japanese incident occurred, the Northeastern government has been destroyed and no longer exists, military police have scattered, rumors have arisen, bandits roam freely, and soldiers and bandits jump over the beams, which are heard from time to time, and the people have lost their wealth and homes, suffering in misery, the state of chaos and the tragic situation is unbearable to witness. Now, fortunately, with the cooperation and support of the gentry and people of Changtu, Lishu, Liaoyuan, Huaide, and Kaiyuan counties, the Sino-Manchurian United Independent Autonomy Association has been established to re-establish all political organs. Therefore, I declare the establishment of the Sino-Manchurian United Independent Autonomy Association, and I hope that all gentry and people will not disregard it, and I pledge to cooperate. I dare to declare, Ma Longtan, Chairman of the Sino-Manchurian United Independent Autonomy Association, October 15, 20th year of the Republic of China.

Martial Law Situation After the Guangzhou Massacre 67

Guangzhou Correspondence: After the bloodbath on Yonghan Road on the night of Double Ten Festival and the expansion of the turmoil, the authorities suspected that the case had some kind of background and immediately issued an emergency martial law order for the entire city. As a result, all those who held a heart full of blood and came out to lead the anti-Japanese and national salvation movement felt apprehensive and fearful. Some stopped their activities, and some disbanded themselves. The vigorous spirit of the people suddenly became depressed after this blow. However, student groups still mustered their remaining courage and persevered until now. The education authorities have earnestly persuaded them, stating that the Yonghan bloodbath should be left to the government to handle, and that the schools should resume classes first and not neglect their studies because of this incident. In recent days, primary and secondary schools have resumed classes one after another. However, Sun Yat-sen University and its affiliated primary and secondary schools are still persisting to the end, insisting on returning to school only after the Yonghan bloodbath is resolved. Therefore, the only ones currently making a final struggle for the Yonghan bloodbath are all the students of the school. The government, seeing that the students of Sun Yat-sen University were so strong in their attitude, feared that there would be other complications, and the martial law order for the entire city has not been lifted. Troops from outside continue to be transferred in to deploy defenses. The 1st Division of the 1st Army under Yu Hanmou has been deployed from Shaoguan to Xiaoping, Jiaheshi, Shangxia Mao, Modao Keng, and the Baiyun Mountain area. The three regiments of the 1st Training Division and the 2nd Regiment of the 2nd Army have been stationed in the eastern suburbs. In the city, in addition to the return of Zhang Da's 5th Division of the 2nd Army under Xiang Hanping, and the deployment of the 3rd Army Li Yangjing Training Division back to the city after the implementation of martial law, Chen Hanguang's entire Guard Brigade returned to the provincial capital from Huangpu on the 15th by order, and stationed in Yonghan Road, Nanguan, and other places. The martial law order is still in effect in the city, and motor vehicles are also difficult to pass at night. All business shops and night markets have been completely closed. The main points of the martial law measures are as follows: (1) Foot patrols are dispatched daily from 7:00 p.m. to 6:00 a.m. the next morning; (2) Citizens' vehicles shall be allowed to travel freely from 7:00 p.m. to 10:00 p.m. (group gatherings without the permission of the martial law commander are prohibited from passing through the martial law area), but they may be checked at any time if they are suspicious; (3) Pedestrian and vehicle traffic is prohibited from 10:00 p.m. to 6:00 a.m. the next morning; (4) Foot patrols shall be stationed at important intersections, crossroads, T-junctions, and busy intersections in each guard area, and the position of the foot patrols shall be determined by the commanders of each unit in consultation with the chief of the public security bureau, and shall be reported to the martial law headquarters; the inspection task shall be carried out by the police under the supervision of the army; (5) Patrol teams shall be dispatched to patrol the roads or inner streets where no foot patrols are stationed; during the martial law period, no officers or soldiers shall leave the camp unless they are on official business or with the permission of their direct superiors. (October 20)

Epidemics Rampant in the Communist Bandit Areas of Jiangxi 68

Six or Seven Thousand People Die in Ningdu Within Ten Days

Nanchang Correspondence: The areas of Yudu, Xingguo, Ningdu, and Huichang in southern Jiangxi have been ravaged by bandits for several years. This summer, after the efforts of the central army to suppress them, they fought in the deep mountains and valleys for three months. The battles of Liantang, Dongcun, Wangbi, Xiaopu, and Longgang were fierce, and the number of deaths and injuries was unprecedented. Corpses littered the fields, and there was no time to bury them, so epidemics were inevitable. According to news from the party-government council, although the main force of the Red bandits has fled far away after Ningdu was recovered by the National Army for the second time, sporadic small groups have not yet been completely eliminated. Therefore, refugees from the surrounding villages are still crowding into the city. After the looting, the displaced people eat wind and sleep in the open, and death from illness is common. The city has a large population, and hygiene is out of the question. Excrement is all over the ground, and garbage is like a mountain, so that epidemics are rampant. In the past ten days, the number of deaths has reached six or seven thousand, mostly wounded soldiers and refugees. There are no coffins to buy, and many are abandoned in the wild. In addition, for dozens of miles around the city, trees and crops have been cut down and burned, and oil, salt, rice, and grain have been looted. A pound of salt sells for as much as one yuan, and the rest can be imagined. It is difficult for the surviving people after the looting to prolong their lives, which is very painful. (October 23)

Epidemics and Bandits Rampant in Northern Jiangsu 69

A Terrible Phenomenon After the Great Flood

Yangzhou Correspondence: Since the breaches in the dykes of the Jianggao counties, the mournful cries have lingered for over two months. Although officials, gentry, and Chinese and foreign philanthropists have repeatedly tried to provide relief to the disaster victims in the affected areas, the disaster area is too large and the situation is unstable, so the order of the Huaiyang area is still difficult to restore to normal. The most unbearable situation is in the Lixiahe area, where epidemics are spreading severely, and it is very difficult to provide medical treatment. Even in the refugee camps in Yangzhou City, with the autumn wind piercing the bones, the number of disaster victims suffering from illness is increasing every day. Yesterday, I passed through the refugee camp in the Xu Gong Temple outside Guangchu Gate and saw that most of the refugees in the camp had a sallow complexion. Of those moaning in the straw piles, five or six out of ten were suffering from dysentery, and the infection was extremely rapid. The sick often could not make it to the toilet and urinated in their pants, and there were many who had no second pair of pants to change into. Therefore, the filthy air was overwhelming, and the infection increased in strength. The illnesses of small children are mostly measles, and deaths are being reported every day. If isolation is not arranged, even non-disaster victims may be affected. The area west of Gaoyou Shaobo Lake was originally a bandit-producing area. Since Zhang Zhijiang's pacification, many bandits have fled to the Anhui border. After this flood, order in various places has inevitably been disrupted, and bandits have taken the opportunity to make a comeback. On the 14th of this month, a large number of local bandits suddenly came to Bian Tang Town in the west of Gaoyou County, looting the town and kidnapping hundreds of meat tickets. Also, in the two counties of Tianchang and Xuyi, which border Jiangsu, many groups of bandits are active. Although the pacification office has sent teams to suppress them, the general public has no livelihood and takes risks.

Page 8

The number of those joining bandit gangs is increasing day by day. If we do not provide both relief and pacification and restore their original occupations, the area will have no peace.

Increased Coal Freight Rates on the Jiaoji Railway 70

Jinan Correspondence: This past summer, the Jiaoji Railway increased coal freight rates by 20%, leading to a strike by coal merchants along the entire line. The railway bureau was forced to rescind the order. Unexpectedly, after a short interval, the old issue has been raised again, with a notice that coal freight rates will again be increased by 20% starting November 1st. Coal merchants along the entire line are greatly alarmed and have risen up in opposition. Zichuan and Boshan, the only coal-producing areas in the province, sent representatives Ding Jingchen, Zhuang Shuting, and others to Jinan to petition Industry Bureau Chief Wang Fangting. Their reasons for opposing the increase are as follows: Now that the Japanese army occupies our Northeast, the whole country is united in resisting Japanese goods and promoting domestic products. The Shanghai anti-Japanese meeting resolved not to purchase Japanese coal and to use domestic coal exclusively, but stipulated that the price of coal should be around twelve taels of silver per ton, and coal merchants should not deliberately raise prices. Currently, the freight cost of transporting coal from Zibo to Qingdao is about four yuan per ton, and the cost of transporting it to Shanghai is already more than twelve taels of silver, making it impossible to compete with coal merchants elsewhere. Now, in the midst of this nationwide resistance against Japanese goods and promotion of domestic products, the Jiaoji Railway is increasing freight rates, not only making them higher than those of any other railway, thus depriving Shandong coal of export opportunities and threatening the livelihood of coal merchants and mine owners, but also contradicting the goal of promoting domestic goods and resisting Japanese goods. Therefore, coal merchants and mine owners along the entire line, standing on the ground of resisting Japan and saving the country, are vehemently opposed to the increase and demand its cancellation, requesting the same treatment as other railways. If the Jiaoji Railway authorities stubbornly ignore this and insist on the increase, they will decide to go on strike until their goal is achieved, and so on. Industry Bureau Chief Wang Fangting indicated that the merchants' stated reasons were indeed valid, but the Jiaoji Railway's action had been approved by the Ministry of Railways and could not be directly intervened. He would forward the matter to the central government, conveying the merchants' suffering and awaiting instructions from the ministry. Currently, the representatives are still in Jinan, contacting local coal merchants to unanimously oppose the increase. Today, I visited representative Ding Jingchen, and according to him, "Zi"chuan, Boshan, Zhangqiu and other counties produce about 3,000 tons of coal per day, of which about 15% is lump coal. In recent years, due to various factors and the high freight rates, users' burdens have increased, and merchants have also experienced difficulties. This past summer, the Jiaoji Railway increased freight rates by 20%, forcing coal merchants to go on strike. The price increase was not mandated by the ministry, and at that time, colleagues went to the ministry to petition, stating that the Jiaoji Railway's freight rates were already higher than those of other railways. All they requested was equal treatment with other railways, or they would rather die in the ministry than leave. Seeing their firm resolve, the Ministry of Railways telegraphed the Jiaoji Railway for a response. Later, colleagues returned to Jinan and met with Ge Guangting, chairman of the Jiaoji Railway Committee. Ge agreed to temporarily not increase prices, but stated that official procedures could not be canceled. Instead, the 20% increase would be changed to a freight rebate returned to coal merchants by the railway bureau (the Jiaoji Railway traditionally reduced freight rates by 20% during the summer when coal merchants' business was poor, calling it a rebate). Afterwards, a fair method would be formulated, and transportation would resume. Unexpectedly, four months later, just as colleagues were hoping for a revised fair method, the Jiaoji Railway again increased freight rates by 20%, directly threatening the livelihood of coal merchants and indirectly blocking Shandong's industry. In reality, even without the increase, the Jiaoji Railway's freight rates are already more than two li higher than those of the Jinpu Railway, making it difficult to compete with coal merchants on other railways. Currently, Shanghai has a resolution to use domestic coal, and Zibo's output could supply it, but due to freight rates, it is impossible. Even within Shandong province, the Yixian Zhongxing Company transports coal to Pukou, a distance of 440 kilometers, at a freight rate of 2.2 yuan, which is 5 li per ton per kilometer. From Jinan to Shanghai, the freight rate is just over one yuan per ton, making the total freight rate to Shanghai less than 3.5 yuan per ton. In contrast, from Zibo to Qingdao is 345 kilometers, with a freight rate of 7.3 li per ton per kilometer, totaling 2.5 yuan per ton. From Qingdao to Shanghai, the freight rate is over three yuan per ton, making the total freight rate to Shanghai over 5.5 yuan per ton. This calculation is based on the freight rates of the Jiaoji Railway before the increase, and it is already impossible for Zibo coal to be transported to Shanghai for sale. Furthermore, considering the market price in Shanghai, current Shanghai coal costs 10 taels and 7.5 qian per ton. Using current freight rates, transporting Zibo coal to Shanghai already requires a loss of 5 jiao per ton. Therefore, coal merchants and mine owners in Zibo cannot accept the 20% increase. However, in these difficult times for the country, they will not easily strike as they did this past summer unless absolutely necessary. They will only reduce production and temporarily maintain the current situation. This measure will inevitably affect users in Qingdao and Jinan, but they have no choice in order to protect their investment." Local correspondence.

Methods for Identifying Suspected Japanese Goods. The Wuxian Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association has spared no effort in inspecting Japanese goods in recent days. Over 500 pieces of Japanese goods have been sealed up, but none have been identified. Merchants are worried about their investments and businesses, and have requested speedy identification and return of non-Japanese goods. The Anti-Japanese Association convened a representative meeting yesterday (25th) and resolved that the sealed Japanese goods would be identified and dealt with. Suspected Japanese goods would be temporarily released to the merchants who provide a shop guarantee and have the industry association and chamber of commerce responsible for them. Samples would be kept for identification. If the goods are found to be Japanese, they will be fined ten times the value of the goods. Future inspections of Japanese goods will be handled in the same manner. Therefore, merchants have been applying for the return of suspected Japanese goods with guarantees.

Wuxi 72

Social Economy in a State of Despair. The harvest in the town this spring, summer, and autumn was poor, and the crops were flooded. The social economy is in a state of panic. In recent months, the silk market has suffered disastrous losses. Factories have suffered heavy losses, with some losing over 100,000 yuan and others losing 40,000 to 50,000 yuan. As a result, they are unable to maintain operations. Factories such as Taifu and Yulun have closed down, and others are raising funds to pay wages in preparation for closure. There are also several factories that are unable to pay wages. Banks and pawnshops have no confidence in recovering their loans. They have been contacting factory managers to discuss repayment plans, but many are avoiding them because the amounts are too large to repay. Loans to the silk, cloth, foreign goods, hardware, electrical materials, and southern goods industries are also unlikely to be repaid because the goods are sealed up and circulation is slow. Therefore, the financial sector is extremely uneasy, and most are collecting money but not lending it. The social economy is in a state of despair.

Husband Catches Wife in Adultery, Wife Attempts Suicide. Mao Shengcai, a resident of No. 12 Shafentuan, Guangfu Gate, works as an accountant at Hongxingsheng Meat Shop near the Great Bridge. His wife, Wang, was unfaithful and had an affair with the landlord, Peng Rulin. They were very intimate, like husband and wife. Yesterday at 9:00 AM, Wang and Rulin were meeting in room 6 of the Park Hotel. While they were being amorous, Mao discovered them and gathered several people to catch them in the act. The adulterer and adulteress were caught on the spot and sent to the First Public Security Bureau for investigation. Wang, feeling ashamed, took off her gold earrings and swallowed them. At 1:00 PM, the chief of the High Branch Bureau prepared a document and sent police to escort her to the General Bureau. Unexpectedly, while passing the New Zhong Bridge, Wang took advantage of a moment of inattention and jumped into the river to commit suicide. Fortunately, she was rescued quickly and did not drown. After arriving at the Public Security Bureau, the department chief questioned her. The adulterer Peng Rulin was detained, Mao Shengcai was ordered to return home, and Mao Wang was sent to the Labor Hospital for treatment. According to the doctor, her life is in danger.

Nantong 73

Former Construction Bureau Chief Flees with Funds, Court Issues Arrest Warrant. After the former Construction Bureau Chief of Nantong, Yao Pengxiong, fled, it was discovered that he had embezzled over 6,000 yuan. The provincial government forwarded the case to the Zhenjiang District Court for arrest. The Zhenjiang court transferred the case file to the Nantong County Court for handling because Yao's crime occurred in Nantong. The County Executive Supervisory Committee Reports Burning of Opium as Fraud. The Nantong County Party Executive Supervisory Committee discovered a major fraud in the burning of opium by the court. Over a thousand taels of opium were missing, and 14.5 jin of fake opium were found. This was shocking, and they have reported it to the province. All sectors are paying close attention to this case.

Yuheng Flour Mill Closes. The Yuheng Flour Mill outside the North Gate of the city has been open for over 20 years, with a capital of 2 million yuan. Its business was very prosperous, and it had distribution points in various counties north of the Yangtze River. The breach in the canal embankment at the North Gate caused the mill to suffer heavy losses. Jin Baojun, a clerk from the High Prosecutor's Office, came to Yangzhou to supervise the burning. Representatives from various organs and groups in the county also attended the event. A total of 4,432 taels of opium, 432 opium bubbles, and 2,688 pieces of opium paraphernalia were burned. Salt Smugglers Rob in Lijiaqiao. In Lijiaqiao, East Township, the county, on the afternoon of the 21st, 40-50 salt smugglers were discovered, each carrying guns, sticks, and clubs, escorting a large amount of smuggled salt. All the shops and residents on the bridge closed their doors to avoid the trouble. Wan Zhishu, who runs a noodle shop, and Kong Shanxiang, a resident, did not have time to open their doors, so the salt smugglers rushed in, overturning chests and cabinets. Wan was robbed of 11 yuan in banknotes and silver dollars (14,500 copper coins) and a noodle-making machine stand. Kong was robbed of a floral cloth quilt, 24 silver dollars, and three fat pigs. The smugglers then left with a roar.

Fire at Tianhou Palace. Last night (23rd) around 7:00 PM, a fire broke out at Yuquanxing Oil Shop on Tianhou Palace Hou Street for unknown reasons. The fire was fierce and unapproachable. It took two hours to extinguish. Over twenty neighboring stores and thirty rooms were burned down, with losses estimated at over 60,000 yuan.

Special Item

Opinions on Relief for the Sixteen Provinces Flood by Xiong Xiling 78

(1) Division of Labor and Cooperation. The scale of the floods in sixteen provinces is broader than the floods in Hebei Province in 1917. Handling it is even more challenging. The Hebei floods in 1917 were managed by a special superintendent appointed by the government, with full power. The governor of the province was only in a supporting role. All relief funds and labor costs were allocated by the central government. The superintendent had the authority to handle transportation, tax exemptions, and rewards and punishments for officials. Therefore, his operation was flexible, and his distribution was thorough. Millions of disaster victims were not frozen or starved. This demonstrates the effectiveness of a single administrative organ. In the case of the floods in the various provinces this time, the central government has established a flood relief committee, and each province has established a branch. This system of collective consultation will inevitably lead to delays, which is an obstacle to the principle of rapid relief. The division of authority between the central government and the provinces is unclear, and responsibilities are not divided. In the future, there will inevitably be mutual shirking, mutual disputes, and mutual blaming. The disaster victims who are crying out for help will suffer in vain. I believe that the central government and local governments should clearly define their respective powers and divide their responsibilities. The central government should be responsible for major construction projects, transportation of relief supplies, tax reductions and exemptions, distribution of relief funds, management of price stabilization, fundraising, and planning strategies. Local governments should be responsible for distributing winter and spring relief, repairing official and private embankments, and all other relief efforts. If the local relief and construction funds are insufficient, the central government can provide subsidies. However, the central government must send personnel to supervise the distribution in order to achieve effective benefits for the people. This method was used by the Superintendent's Office for the floods in the capital area in 1917. Local gentry and charitable organizations have close relationships with the local community and religious beliefs, which are better than those of officials. Secondly, because the disaster area is too large, the central government does not have enough talent to employ. Therefore, a compromise was adopted. The Superintendent's Office proposed relief funds of over one million yuan and entrusted the Shunzhi Relief Bureau to distribute winter relief, and proposed 500,000 yuan to entrust the Zhili Righteous Relief Bureau to distribute spring relief, and proposed 900,000 yuan to subsidize various miscellaneous relief efforts. The Superintendent's Office also assigned relief investigation committee members to go to the disaster area with the gentry to review the severity of the disaster, and then assigned relief supervision committee members to supervise the distribution to verify that there were no irregularities in the relief funds. Furthermore, fearing that the above two committee members might be biased or derelict in their duties, the president was requested to appoint special inspectors to visit and investigate whether the assigned committee members were performing their duties. Therefore, although the Superintendent's Office released over 2.4 million yuan in relief funds, it did not directly handle a single penny of the distribution. Secondly, for river works, due to the lack of talent at that time, it was necessary to continue to use the experience and skilled workers of the old river workers. However, fearing that they would repeat their old habits due to accumulated malpractices, when the River Bureau submitted the estimated work budget, the chairman of the Five Great River Survey and Defense Committee was first sent with the committee members to inspect the estimated work budget and the needs for blocking and building. Once the estimated calculation was finalized, the funds were allocated, and the committee members for supervising the project and inspecting the project were sent to supervise whether the project was verified and free from irregularities. During the autumn flood season, supervisory committee members were sent to work to check whether the river committee members were performing their duties. Those who were found to be fraudulent or incompetent were severely punished at any time to serve as a warning to others. Therefore, although the flood this year rose sharply, the Five Great Rivers were able to celebrate safety because of this. However, there was also a notable feature at the time, that is, the chairmen of the committees supervising the various works were all military personnel, and the assistants accompanying the practice were all students from the Southern Haihe Engineering School and the Shandong Engineering Bureau. They were able to endure hardship, overcome sentimentality, and were more responsible than other officials. This is the past experience of river works for the floods in Hebei Province. This time, the disaster has affected several provinces, and it is even more necessary to distinguish the powers and responsibilities of the central government and local governments in order to have the benefit of division of labor and cooperation.

(2) Division of Miscellaneous Relief. The vastness of the disaster areas and the large number of disaster victims in the sixteen provinces are several times greater than in Hebei Province in 1917. Relying solely on the financial and human resources of the central government is insufficient to cope. Moreover, construction relief only covers the able-bodied, and the elderly and weak will inevitably be left out. Direct relief only covers winter and spring, while production must also be taken into account. In 1917, the central government allocated only over 2.4 million yuan for the floods in Hebei Province, while the number of miscellaneous relief efforts independently organized by various counties and the number of charitable groups reached over 2 million yuan. This is the efficiency of division of labor. The following are about nine items that were handled:

First, price stabilization. After the flood, grain merchants and wealthy families inevitably stockpiled and increased prices. The poorest and next poorest relied on relief, and middle-class households who could buy food were also in trouble. Therefore, there must be price stabilization. However, because the disaster area is vast, the key is for merchants to be greedy for high prices and transport more grain to ensure a continuous supply. If you rely solely on central and local government officials to stabilize prices, you will not only lack the power to supply the entire area, but you will also fear that the pricing will be too low, which will hinder the source of commercial goods. Therefore, the price of this price stabilization can only be slightly lower than the price of commercial goods by two coins to prevent it from rising, but not to prevent the arrival of goods. Therefore, although the central government stipulated that 500,000 shi of grain should be stabilized in price in 1917, the result was that only over 84,000 shi were transported, and over 858,000 yuan was spent, and the market price was flat. This was all due to the slightly lower pricing and the large amount of commercial goods transported.

Second, coal relief. After the flood, all the grasses were submerged, and fuel became a problem for the people. Although there was grain relief, it was difficult to eat without fuel. The south mostly used firewood, and the poor had no money to buy it. Therefore, this item is indispensable. In addition to the 10,000 tons purchased and transported by the Superintendent's Office in Hebei Province in 1917, various coal mining companies donated thousands of tons and distributed them to 41 counties. This time, the large coal mining companies in the north and south should be urged to donate coal to the best of their ability to complete this task.

Third, loans. After the flood, small-scale industrial and commercial businesses in various cities and counties were trapped. If methods are not taken to help them, they will inevitably become unemployed. In Hebei Province in 1917, the majority of the 100,000 households in the eight counties of Gaoyang, Baoding, Raoyang, Tianjin, Renqiu, and Suning Li were engaged in weaving. Each household has an average of five people, which is 500,000 people. If they lose their jobs due to the disaster, not only will production be reduced, but the weaving machines will also be at risk. Therefore, the Superintendent's Office borrowed 1 million yuan in yarn from the spinning company and distributed it to the cloth merchants to distribute to the weavers without interest, so that the livelihood of these 100,000 households could be protected. The yarn price was recovered in full the following year. The government only spent tens of thousands of yuan in interest. This time, there are many small industrial and commercial businesses in the various provinces and ports. The central government should discuss with the Shanghai banking groups to raise huge amounts of money to form a lending bank and use the above method to help countless small businesses. According to the large disaster area and the large number of disaster victims this time, it is estimated that at least 10,000 yuan of various bank notes held by those affected by the flood have been submerged and lost. It is also natural for banks to fulfill this obligation. In addition, the profit bureau can also order each county to imitate the practices of Hebei Province in 1917, which collected funds and established 309 offices, which were helpful to small industrial and commercial businesses.

Fourth, righteous pawnshops. After the flood, the small farmers in the villages were particularly poor. Although they had several acres of land to sell, they had no money to cultivate it. How could they survive? They must establish righteous pawnshops to allow them to mortgage their real estate. A total of 29 were established in various counties of Hebei Province in 1917. In the years of famine in Shanxi Province, the provincial government formulated regulations ordering each county to instruct the wealthy households in their villages or the wealthy households in neighboring villages that were not affected by the disaster to mortgage the real estate, which was very effective after the autumn harvest. The China Foreign Famine Relief Commission has operated credit cooperatives in Hebei to provide mutual assistance lending methods, which can also be adopted. (To be continued)

Wang Jingwei's Statement Yesterday 84

Wang Jingwei made the following statement yesterday: "Mr. Chiang's telegram of resignation and the telegram of the abolition of the Guangzhou National Government have the greatest significance in bringing an end to the disputes of the past few years and ushering in a new era from now on. What are the characteristics of this new era? Although it is difficult to say in one sentence, its greatest significance is to liberate politics from the control of military forces. Politics under the control of military forces will never have good politics. No matter what kind of military forces, they cannot be allowed to control politics. This is the dividing line between modern countries and barbaric countries. In barbaric countries, there must be special forces, especially military forces, to seize power. In modern countries, as long as you get the trust of the people, you can seize power without military forces, especially without military forces. Active military personnel must resign from their active military positions if they want to engage in politics. Only in this way can they avoid holding military forces to threaten politics. In modern countries, active military personnel are absolutely trusted by the people because they are focused on national defense. National defense is absolutely necessary, so active military personnel are also absolutely trusted by the people. As for engaging in politics, there will inevitably be political enemies, because political views are relative, not absolute. Understanding this point, you can know that no matter how transcendent a person is, he cannot take care of both military and political affairs at the same time.

All Employees of the Zhonghua Book Company Go on Strike Yesterday 91

More than a Thousand People in the Main Factory and Distribution Center

Because the Management Refused to Allow Li Hongbin to Return to Work

More than a thousand employees of the main factory and distribution center of the Zhonghua Book Company in this city went on strike unanimously yesterday afternoon because the management violated government orders and refused to allow workers to return to work. The situation is very serious. The details of each item are recorded below.

Reasons for the Strike 92

Li Hongbin, an officer of the Zhonghua Book Company branch of the Municipal Publishing Industry Trade Union, was dismissed by the management. On the 22nd, the trade union received an order from the Social Bureau approving his return to work. Representatives Wang Wenhua and Wang Yongliang of the trade union, holding the approval, together with Yang Yinlin and Wang Jiping, officers of the Social Bureau's office, contacted Chen Xiegong and Wang Jinshi, the directors of the factory and distribution center. Chen and Wang stated that General Manager Lu Feikui had not been notified in advance and could not allow him to return to work. Later, Wang Wenhua went to the Social Bureau for instructions, and Wang Bin was sent to the factory as a representative, scolding Wang Jinshi face to face, saying that the factory must abide by the government's approval order and allow Li to return to work tomorrow. The director readily agreed, but unexpectedly, when Li Hongbin went to return to work on the 23rd, the factory refused again. The workers of the factory were very angry that the factory dared to defy government laws and regulations, so they spontaneously went on strike at 4 pm the day before yesterday.

Employees' Congress 93

All employees of the Zhonghua Book Company distribution center on Fourth Malu held an emergency meeting of members inside the distribution center at 11:30 am yesterday to discuss the case of the management defying government orders and refusing to allow worker Li Hongbin to return to work. Lu Zhonglun was elected chairman, and reported on the entire process of the strike by all workers in the main factory. The atmosphere at the scene was very tense. It was immediately resolved that: (1) Starting today, responding to the main factory, all will automatically go on strike; (2) Refuse customers politely; (3) Strictly maintain order.

Overall Strike 94

More than 800 workers in the main factory of the Zhonghua Book Company on Jing'an Temple Road spontaneously went on strike at 4 pm the day before yesterday because they opposed the management violating the Social Bureau's order and refusing to allow trade union officer Li Hongbin to return to work. Yesterday was Sunday, which was a regular holiday, and today the strike continues. More than 130 employees of the Fourth Malu distribution center, after a general meeting, unanimously went on strike at 1 pm yesterday when business hours started. Slogans were posted on the gate and windows, such as "Today's strike, customers please forgive us," "Li Hongbin will not return to work, we will not work," "We want to protect government laws and regulations," and so on.

Group Leaders' Petition 95

The Zhonghua Book Company branch of the Publishing Industry Trade Union submitted ten conditions for improving treatment three months ago. After repeated mediation by the Social Bureau, it was impossible to resolve them because the management refused to attend, and the mediation was declared unsuccessful and submitted to arbitration. At 10 am the day before yesterday, more than a hundred group leaders and officers went to the Municipal Government to petition, demanding prompt arbitration. Secretary-General Yu Hongjun received them and promised to arbitrate within the next week.

Management's Attitude 96

A reporter from the New Sound News Agency visited Xue Ji'an, director of the distribution center of the bureau, yesterday and asked for the company's opinion on the employees' strike. According to him, after the employees went on strike, he reported the situation to General Manager Lu Fei Bohong for verification and handling. The worker Li Hongbin of the main factory was actually dismissed for violating the rules and fighting with workers in the same factory. After the employees of the distribution center went on strike today, customers hesitated and business declined greatly. Fortunately, it is now the off-season, and the daily loss is only about a thousand yuan, he said.

Establishment of the Third Regiment of the Volunteer Army 97

Serial Numbers Issued Yesterday

The National Salvation Volunteer Army of this city has been established, and officers have also been appointed. The regimental commander is Zheng Xingli, the first battalion commander is Chen Weizhong (under the jurisdiction of the entire battalion of the Maya Silk Factory Volunteer Army), the second battalion commander is Zhu Lin, and the third battalion commander is Wu Jiansheng. At 8 am yesterday, the first gathering and mobilization speech was held at the Nanshi Public Stadium. About a thousand people, including various committee members, officers, and volunteers, attended. Committee member Chen Ya'fu and regimental commander Zheng Xingli gave speeches one after another (the words are omitted). After the speech, serial numbers were issued and the meeting was dismissed. It was decided that training would begin tomorrow. It is said that the first battalion will train at the Maya Main Factory on Rihui East Road, the second battalion will train at the Nanshi Public Stadium, and the third battalion will train at three locations: the Qingyun Road training ground in Zhabei, the Nanshi Public Stadium, and the Zhenhua School on Qiqihar Road.

Anti-Japanese Work in All Circles

Merchants Voluntarily Seal Up Japanese Goods 98

Wu Banjiang, a member of the Japanese Goods Inspection Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Citizens' Federation, together with Chen Guangxin and other members of the Ninth District Branch, began inspecting Japanese goods yesterday. At the Ruiyuanxiang Foreign Goods General Store and branch on Zhejiang Road, Yongyuanxiang Foreign Goods Store on Avenue Edward VII, the Cooperative Store, Xinyitai Store, Xiangchang Native Products Store, Zhentai Porcelain Store, Tiandetang Pharmacy, Zhicheng Printing House, Fukang Native Products Store, Zhu Fuxing Store, Wanshunxiang Sock Factory, Hengxingchang Foreign Goods Store, and others, many kinds of Japanese goods were sealed up. The guest merchants filled out voluntary statements of never buying or selling Japanese goods to express their determination to sever economic relations with Japan forever. Before inspecting and sealing the Japanese goods, the merchants had already packed the hateful goods into boxes to wait for the inspection committee to seal them up. This kind of spontaneous patriotic enthusiasm is truly admirable.

Equal Emphasis on Resisting Japanese Goods and Promoting National Goods 99

The Wuhu Cloth Industry Guild believes that resisting Japanese goods and promoting national goods should be given equal emphasis. Fearing that national cloth head ends might contain Japanese raw materials and be detained by the anti-Japanese association, the guild specially sent Cui Haixiang and Huang Xiren to Shanghai to personally investigate. It is now known that Cui and Huang arrived in Shanghai yesterday and went to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the National Goods Factory Federation to request assistance in introducing them to visit factories for on-the-spot investigations.

All the members of the Students Studying at the Japanese Military Academy Who Withdrew from School to Save the Country, more than 170 people, have all arrived in Shanghai. Zhu Zhaoxin Arrives in Shanghai in Response to a Summons 101

Expected to Go to Beijing by Overnight Train Tonight

Zhu Zhaoxin, former Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs and Minister to England and Italy, arrived in Shanghai on the Russian Empress ship on the 25th of this month. A reporter from the New Sound News Agency met him at the pier and had a conversation with him, which is excerpted below: (Question) What is the purpose of your trip, sir? (Answer) I received a telegram from the Central Political Conference appointing me as a member of the Special Committee on Foreign Affairs. I am going to Beijing to attend. (Question) Have you held any positions in Guangdong in recent years? (Answer) I have been living at home in Guangdong with my mother and have not held any position. Now that the national crisis is increasingly urgent, I have come upon summons, hoping to contribute my years of diplomatic experience. (Question) I heard that the Central Government will reappoint you to an important foreign affairs position, is that true? (Answer) I have no knowledge of that. (Question) If that happens, would you be happy to accept it? (Answer) The purpose of my trip is not to seek office, but to participate in the discussions on foreign affairs and express my views based on my experience. I will be satisfied with that. (Question) Will you be visiting the important figures in Shanghai? (Answer) I have to go to the capital immediately and do not have time to visit everyone. I also do not want to disturb people in my busy schedule. (Question) You used to be the chief representative of the League of Nations and are very familiar with the situation of the League. What are your opinions on the League's handling of the Manchurian issue this time? Can you tell me? (Answer) I have my own plans and will present them to the Special Committee on Foreign Affairs. I should not publish them at this time. (Question) Japan does not listen to the advice of the League of Nations, and a rupture between China and Japan is inevitable. I would like to hear your opinion, sir. (Answer) This matter is of great importance and I do not want to express my opinion rashly, he said. It is said that Mr. Zhu is scheduled to take the Beijing-Shanghai night train tonight to go to Beijing and participate in the foreign affairs discussion meeting.

Second Group of Refugees from the Shenyang Arsenal Arrives in Shanghai 102

Forming a Maintenance Group to Petition the Municipal Government

After the violent Japanese army occupied Liaoning, the machinery, raw materials, guns, and bullets of the Shenyang Arsenal were all moved away by the Japanese army, and all personnel were forced to leave the factory. The second group arrived in Shanghai a few days ago and formed a maintenance group to petition. The first group of personnel sent a telegram to Mayor Zhang yesterday, requesting placement. The Arsenal Department is now working on finding placements. The details of each item are recorded below.

Second Group Arrives in Shanghai 103

The second group of refugees from the Shenyang Arsenal, who arrived in Shanghai on October 20th, a total of 260 people, are temporarily living in the Qu Zhenren Temple in Gaochang Temple. They formed a maintenance group and held a general meeting at 8 am the day before yesterday. After the meeting, the entire group went to the Municipal Government to petition, requesting (1) maintenance of food and (2) placement of work. Municipal Government Counselor Sun Baozhen received them and ordered them to go to the National Government Relief Committee regarding the maintenance of food, and promised to telegraph the Military and Political Department's Arsenal Department regarding the placement of work. The entire group was satisfied and returned. In the afternoon, representatives Song Shaofu, Chen Zailiang, Fan Yaozhang, Yu Guanlin, etc. were appointed to request maintenance from the National Government Relief Committee. The Relief Committee agreed to give each person a relief payment of four yuan, as in the case of the first group.

Telegraph Requesting Placement 104

The first group of refugees sent a telegram yesterday, saying, "Most Urgent, Respectfully Addressed to Mayor Zhang of the Shanghai Municipal Government, We, the group, petitioned a few days ago, and you kindly forwarded the telegram to the Military and Political Department to find a factory for assignment, and directed us to the Water Disaster Relief Association, which thankfully gave each person four yuan, maintaining our current livelihood. We members are grateful beyond measure. However, we have found that the relief funds of the association come from donations, dividing a cup of soup among many people, filling our empty stomachs. Although it is unavoidable, it is emotionally difficult. Who has no conscience and can not feel ashamed? Furthermore, although we members lack outstanding skills, we still have our strengths. We have been in the factory for many years and have a wealth of experience. At this time of national crisis, military equipment is essential, and it is even more necessary to preserve arsenal personnel. Moreover, since our factory has been occupied by the Japanese and the Han factory has just started construction, there are not many existing factories and limited output. Once we go to war with the enemy, we are afraid that there will be a shortage of guns, ammunition, and explosives. As mere laborers, we members have no ability to change things. However, if the country wants to resist foreign aggression, it is not appropriate to ignore this talent for expanding military equipment. We have been waiting for more than ten days, and the reply telegram is still silent. We have no choice but to be anxious. We believe that the Mayor is a famous expert in industry and a pioneer in the labor world. Even though you are now dedicated to municipal administration, you have a clear understanding of the national crisis and the plight of the workers. What is there to say? Since you kindly telegraphed us before, we will seek your continued safety and telegraph you again, so that you can assign us to a factory as soon as possible, so that we will not be delayed in Shanghai for a long time, relying on the second-hand relief. If the Military Department agrees, we vow to work hard on the one hand, manufacturing military equipment, and on the other hand, publicize our suffering to the workers, inspiring public loyalty, in order to be the pioneers of courage and the rear shield against Japan. This is the responsibility that we members should fulfill, and it is also the only way to repay your kindness. The Eastern Province Arsenal Refugees Petition Maintenance Group Chief Supervisor and Clerk Li Tiechen, Representatives Dai Xiuzhai, Wang Wenlong, She Guilin, Zhang Longshun, together with all the members, respectfully kowtow, respectfully kowtow."

Case of Japanese Residents Shooting and Wounding Chinese Police 105

Representations from Anti-Japanese Associations of Various Universities

Huadong News Agency reports that Japanese residents Nishimura Matsumoto and others, on the night of the 21st of this month, provoked trouble and shot and wounded police officer Wang Changshun of the Municipal Public Security Bureau on Le'an Road and East Yokohama Road. After detailed investigation by the Municipal Government, a serious protest was lodged with the Japanese Consulate. The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Federation of Students from various universities in this port, because this case occurred in the Public Concession, specially sent a letter to Mr. Fessenden, Secretary-General of the Public Works Department, yesterday, inquiring about everything and hoping that the Public Works Department will guarantee that such incidents will not happen again in the future. Representatives Nie Haifan and Hu Wenquan were also sent to the Municipal Government to visit Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, requesting serious negotiations. The original text of their letter to Fessenden is recorded below: "Respectfully Sir, according to news reports, Japanese people committed violence in North Sichuan Road, shooting and wounding police officer Wang Changshun, which is shocking to hear. We have investigated the duties of your bureau, which are to maintain law and order. This time, Japanese people rioted, and you failed to prevent it in advance and failed to stop it afterwards, resulting in this unfortunate incident. Furthermore, the murderer was arrested on the spot but was released without legal sanctions. What is your bureau's responsibility for encouraging thugs to run rampant and endangering the people? We hope that you will reply and that your bureau will absolutely guarantee that such incidents will not happen again in the future. We are sending this letter in response and hope that you will investigate and take action, Fessenden of the Public Works Department."

Zhang Yaozeng's Letter to the People of the Country (3) 106

All of my unemployed countrymen, if you have assets, then donate to military needs, relieve disasters, create businesses, and harmonize society. All speculative and lewd lifestyles must be strictly eliminated. If you have no assets, then invigorate your spirits, endure hardships, and sell your labor, or serve on the front lines, or seek work. As long as there is an effective place, do not ask about the advantages and disadvantages of treatment. All wandering and troublemaking lifestyles must be strictly eliminated. All of my countrymen who are engaged in academic pursuits, if you are in a teaching position, then strictly correct the academic atmosphere, honestly purchase and teach, and cultivate knowledgeable and capable talents. At the same time, strive to improve and create new frontiers in scholarship to guide people's lives and increase social utility. General students should be humble and self-respecting, strenuously avoid floating and frivolousness, and practice their patriotic work from reading and being a person. Intensify the cultivation of intelligence to be a tool for subduing the enemy. Intensify physical training so that they have the qualifications to serve on the battlefield in the end. Those who are like this are called total national mobilization. With China's vast land and large population, if total national mobilization is carried out, what is unbreakable, let alone Japan? However, our nation's resistance to violent Japan also has its own meaning and boundaries, which must be carefully considered. First, self-defense. As humanity evolves, all nations are only allowed to govern and defend themselves and are not allowed to infringe upon each other. Japan, regardless of the destruction of public reason, rampantly carries out aggression. My countrymen should each implement total mobilization, taking any effective means for self-defense. However, the purpose is only self-defense, so if Japan can repent and completely withdraw its aggression and compensate for the losses, then our country does not necessarily have to resort to arms. Even if violent Japan persists in its delusion, and we have no choice but to resort to arms, it should naturally be limited to completely eliminating its aggression and compensating for our losses. Excessive oppression and local retaliation are certainly not allowed. Second, safeguarding human civilization. Humanity has been blindly walking in the dark night for a long time. After the World War, a glimmer of dawn was seen, knowing that private wars should be eliminated and culture should be developed together. Therefore, international efforts to maintain peace and international systems to maintain peace have been gradually emphasized, such as the League of Nations, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and the agreement on reducing armaments. These are the sprouts of this trend, and the future is still far away. Japan suddenly cannot restrain itself and wants to destroy it, making humanity return to the black night. This is truly a great threat to human culture, how can it only be a harm to my Chinese nation? All nations moving toward civilization have a great responsibility to correct and salvage it. How can it be that only my nation should resist it? The reason why our country does not hastily declare war on Japan, but firmly requests the League of Nations to impose sanctions, is not out of self-preservation, nor out of dependence. It is temporarily enduring its own humiliation to maintain the new opportunities for humanity that are about to be cut off, and to supervise the comrades of various countries to give full play to the practical effects of the new structure of civilization. Therefore, while my countrymen are implementing total mobilization, they should still cooperate with the League of Nations, relying on its organization and strength, to restore justice and maintain peace. If the League of Nations is equal to a void, and the countries cannot uphold justice strictly or cannot resolutely exert their strength, then my nation, for the sake of the future of human civilization, should go to war, even with a single horse and a tattered gun, without hesitation. This is also the attitude that my countrymen should adopt. Alas, survival and defeat, prosperity and ruin, the crisis is imminent. All of my countrymen have a heart to sacrifice themselves and save the country, but if they do not act in the right way, they will only increase the disasters. In my humble opinion, the only way is to truly awaken, truly unite, and implement total national mobilization to defend ourselves and protect human civilization. There is no better way than this. I, Yaozeng, am clumsy and unskilled. I used to participate in the great government and had many views on sovereignty. In recent years, I have been living by my own efforts at sea, preserving my life. I am indifferent to the order and chaos of national affairs. When I reflect on myself in the quiet night, I am also one of the people who caused the chaos and weakness. Encountering this national crisis, I dare not avoid taboos again and remain silent. I sincerely disclose what I have seen in my conscience to all my countrymen. If I am pardoned and deeply reflect upon it, it would be fortunate indeed. Furthermore, I attach to this that my writing of this book is purely motivated by a sincere concern for the country. I not only have absolutely no hope for political power, but also do not participate in any internal political movements. What I hold to join the total mobilization and serve the country is only the two things mentioned above: diligently studying academics and supporting public opinion. I also express this to the workers for their appraisal. Zhang Yaozeng, October 21, 20th year.

The aggressive Manchuria-Mongolia policy of the Japanese Tanaka Cabinet is the basis for repeated acts of violence by the Japanese army in China. The third edition, commissioned for printing, has tens of thousands of copies and will begin printing on November 1. If various circles want to include their printing, they must contact the New Sound News Agency on the third floor of the Daxin Silk Store on Hankou Road and Shilu Road before October 31. Special Meeting of Directors and Managers of Japanese Textile Mills 109

No Concrete Results

The Continental News reported that the directors and managers of various Japanese textile mills in this port held a special meeting yesterday (the 24th) afternoon at the Japanese Club to report on the situation and discuss countermeasures to the Chinese economic boycott. The meeting was chaired by Mr. Funatsu, the director of the Textile Industry Association in China. It is said that the meeting did not produce any concrete results and will be reconvened on Wednesday. Afterwards, Funatsu told a reporter from the newspaper that he could not accurately inform when the Japanese textile mills in China would close down and how they would close down. However, if the situation deteriorates, all the Japanese textile mills may be forced to close down one after another. Although this step is regrettable, it is inevitable if the Chinese economic boycott movement does not subside. At present, some Japanese residents in this port are strongly advising the managers of Japanese textile mills to close down the mills as a countermeasure to the Chinese economic boycott. Today (the 24th) afternoon, they also sent several representatives to ask for my opinion on this. I frankly described the current situation of each factory, but because the path to be taken requires careful consideration, I could not make any concrete statements, he said.

Current Status of Silk Factories' Decline 112

Extremely Weak Overseas Sales

Closures Occurring One After Another

There are a total of 106 silk factories in the Chinese and foreign concessions of this city. European and American factory silk sales are extremely weak. When the new silk came on the market, only thirty to forty factories reluctantly started work. The issuance of the Jiangsu and Zhejiang silk industry public bonds, the silk factories in the three districts of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai went to the custody committee to collect them, and the number reached 98%. Only one or two factories in each district did not collect them due to certain matters. However, the silk market remains sluggish. It's a drop in the bucket and does not help. Only about ten to twenty Shanghai silk factories are trying to resume work, and there are more than sixty in total. Recently, due to overseas economic instability, Japanese silk is cheap and selling strongly. White factory silk does not sell in England and France, and American merchants depress prices and purchase cheaply. The price of electric spun silk is very small, but the cost of silk is still high. Each bale must lose one to two hundred taels. In the past, there were silk cocoon leftovers sold to Japanese merchants, which could be used to make up for the losses. Since the severance of relations with Japan, the leftovers have been sluggish. The factory losses are even greater and cannot be supported. The number of factories reducing work and closing down is increasing day by day. The silk factory industry is in danger and has fallen into an irreversible situation. Currently, only thirty to forty silk factories in Shanghai are operating, and seven or eight of them are stopping and starting from time to time. Only more than twenty factories in Wuxi are operating, and most of the factories that are operating are preparing to suspend work temporarily in order to preserve their strength. The precarious situation of the silk factory industry is even more tragic.

Record of the Jiangsu Rice United Association Regular Meeting 113

The Jiangsu Ninghu Municipal and County Rice Industry Association Joint Association held its fifth executive and supervisory committee regular meeting at Cuixiu at 2:00 PM yesterday. Zhu Zixiang was elected chairman, and formalities were observed. The chairman reported that the previous proposal on the illegal levy of rice donations by the Liyang County Government had been answered by the Provincial Government, stating that the Department of Civil Affairs had been instructed to investigate and verify. Also, the request submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau to allow Jiangsu rice transport ships to pass through Zhejiang had been approved by the Bureau. The Municipal Government approved the response from the Zhejiang Provincial Government regarding the permission for rice boats to pass through Zhejiang, and has ordered the Department of Civil Affairs to investigate and handle the case together. Furthermore, the Changshu Rice Industry Association's request to prevent the Rice Transport Merchant Ship United Association from registering has also been approved by the Social Affairs Bureau, stating that it has requested the Public Security Bureau to order the subordinate authorities to stop the Rice Transport Merchant Ship United Association from registering and to instruct the association to submit a report on its organizational history for review. Subsequently, the Wuxi Soybean and Rice Industry Association and Committee Member Yan Xiaoquan's proposal to request investigations in various places to compare the profits and losses of this year's autumn harvest for reference was discussed. It was resolved to immediately issue investigation forms to the members present, requesting them to fill them out in detail and report to the association. The chairman temporarily proposed that the violent actions of Japan have not been resolved, and if military force is used, the food problem will be the first to be affected. Adjusting surpluses and deficits is of utmost importance. It is proposed that members of the association conduct a thorough investigation of the autumn harvest situation and submit a report to the authorities for overall planning to prepare for it. It was resolved to submit a report to the authorities after each member submits their investigation report.

Coal Industry Held an Emergency Meeting Yesterday 114

Pledged Never to Buy or Sell Japanese Goods

Requested Various Agencies to Relieve the Coal Shortage

The Municipal Coal Industry Association convened an emergency general meeting of members at 11:00 AM yesterday at the Coal Industry Office on Fuyou Road. Chairman Chen Yushu presided over the meeting and resolved the following issues: (1) Should registered Japanese goods be sealed up? It was resolved that goods registered before September 30 would be allowed to be used through accommodation. From October 1, all Japanese goods will not be allowed to be bought or sold. (2) Pledged never to buy or sell Japanese goods forever. It was resolved that the original text of the oath would be revised to exclude registered Japanese coal and the rest would be passed. (3) How to transport domestic coal to Shanghai for relief? It was resolved to report the number of coal reserves in this city to the Ministry of Industry of the National Government and various agencies, requesting assistance and distribution. The date and source cannot be determined because there are no ships or vehicles for transportation. Please provide vigorous assistance to the above agencies, otherwise, the association will not be responsible for any coal shortages that may occur in the future. The meeting adjourned after the agenda was completed.

Member's Oath: I swear that from today onwards, except for the registered Japanese coal, I will never buy or sell Japanese goods, and I will lead my family members to widely persuade relatives and friends to implement it consistently. If there is any violation, I am willing to accept the most severe punishment. Sincerely swear.

Huibridge at the Border of Shangsong is About to Be Built

The construction of roads, culverts, and bridges, etc., on the Beihui County Road built by the Shanghai County Government is nearing completion, and the entire road can be opened to traffic soon. Translated International Relations Theory 118

All Three Volumes Now Available

The International Relations Theory, co-translated by Zeng Yusheng and Ye Qifang, is originally written by the first-class international political scientist Peel in the United States. It was once popular after publication and recognized as one of the famous works. Now, the two gentlemen Zeng have translated it into Chinese, a total of three volumes. It has now been published in succession by Shenzhou Guoguang Press. Anyone who is concerned about the international situation should have one.

(5) The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association sent a letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to solicit donations for operating expenses, which will be started after the flood donation is over. (6) The association's operating funds were sent to the Caojiadu Shaoxing Wine Inspection Office to spend dozens of yuan for assistance. All six items were passed unanimously, and the meeting adjourned.

Spring Chair Industry: The Spring Chair Industry Association held an emergency meeting of all representatives the other day. Chairman Wang Quanxing discussed: (1) Japan disregarded the League of Nations, proposed unconditional conditions, and coerced consent. How should this be expressed? It was resolved: (A) to send a telegram to the representatives to withdraw from the League of Nations; (B) to send a telegram to the central government to declare war on Japan. (2) Economic severance is a non-violent war. If we persist to the end, we will surely put the Japanese in a desperate situation. It should be implemented. It was resolved to notify all members and inform all employees that if they purchase Japanese goods again, their positions will be immediately terminated. (3) The association should establish an Anti-Japanese National Salvation Volunteer Army to go to the national disaster together. It was resolved to notify all members to register with the association immediately. The rest was omitted.

Opening the Sluice Gate to Release Water is Not Accurate 123

Reply from the Jiangsu Provincial Government

Opening the sluice gate to release water and blocking the breach is not a good idea. The association recently telegraphed the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Jiangbei Canal Post-Disaster Engineering Committee to inquire whether there is such a method. The reply is as follows: Wang, Huang Cheng, and other gentlemen of the Jiangsu Flood Relief Charity Association: I have received your telegram. The dike-blocking project has already been implemented. The five major breaches can be closed next month, and there is no discussion of opening the sluice gate to release water. As for closing the Sanhekou breach, we will discuss it with the Huai River Management Committee and the Lianghuai Canal Envoy in order to save lake water to aid spring navigation and irrigation. Please release your worries. Sincerely, The Canal Engineering Post-Disaster Committee.
